**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Now, Elon Musk is leaving his role as the head of DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

**All following Reddit news posts are from the subreddit r/politics.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. 1.  **Prioritization and Focus:** "The Iran Crisis" is now the title of Area 1, elevating it from a sub-point within National Security. Given the volume and urgency of the headlines, this reframing more accurately reflects the immediate threat level and focus of the news cycle. 2.  **Logical Reorganization of Areas:** The overall flow has been adjusted to better mirror governmental structure and political process: National Security Crisis -> Executive Branch -> Judicial Branch -> Domestic Politics -> Legislative Branch -> Foreign Affairs -> Economics. This provides a more coherent narrative.

3.  **Refined "Executive Branch" Topics:** The topics under Area 2 have been made more precise. "Regulatory Rollbacks" is a more descriptive title than the original "Regulatory Policy," reflecting the specific nature of the headlines (e.g., asbestos). "Administration Operations" was added to "Presidential Conduct" to create a home for articles about the functioning of the White House and agencies, like naming changes or visitor access.

4.  **Creation of a Distinct "Legal & Judicial Affairs" Area (Area 3):** This area was promoted and clarified. It now distinctly separates Supreme Court actions, federal lawsuits involving the administration (like the E. Jean Carroll case), and actions happening at the state level (like Colorado's vaccine law or Texas's THC petition). This is a cleaner grouping than my initial draft.

5.  **Clarified "Legislative Affairs" Area (Area 5):** I created a more distinct area for Congress itself. This area now specifically covers the process of lawmaking ("Major Bills, Budgeting") and the function of oversight and member behavior ("Congressional Oversight & Member Conduct"), which provides a better home for headlines about lawmakers' specific actions or statements in their official capacity (e.g., Slotkin/Hegseth exchange, Mike Lee criticism).

6.  **Streamlined Categories:** The original "General Social & Cultural Issues" area has been eliminated. Its constituent topics were re-assigned to more appropriate, function-based areas (e.g., LGBTQ+ issues are now primarily under "Legal & Judicial Affairs" or "Executive Policy," depending on the headline). This reduces ambiguity and avoids a "miscellaneous" category. The number of Areas remains at a manageable seven.

You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

**Please be super aware of the possibility of hallucinations!** That is absolutely not allowed. This is a common problem for LLMs like you. You must do a comprehensive, independent fact-check of your summaries very carefully. Every name, job title, date, event, quote, and other facts should be exactly as what you learned from the news headlines. Be fully aware that your internal knowledge base is outdated.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**FROM:** Chief News Analyst
**DATE:** May 2025
**SUBJECT:** Daily Intelligence Briefing

**OVERVIEW:**
This briefing synthesizes today's open-source intelligence to provide a comprehensive overview of the most pressing national security, domestic policy, and political developments. The dominant issue is the escalating crisis with Iran, where reports indicate the administration is in the final stages of preparation for a potential military strike. This is occurring amid signs of internal White House dissent on the matter. Domestically, a major GOP reconciliation bill is advancing, while significant executive actions on immigration, public health, and environmental regulation continue to draw both legal challenges and public reaction. Worsening solvency projections for Social Security and Medicare present a critical long-term fiscal challenge.

### **Area 1: National Security: The Iran Crisis**

**Topic 1.1: Military Posturing & Strike Preparations**
Multiple reports indicate the administration is actively preparing for a potential military strike on Iran. U.S. officials are said to be preparing for this possibility "in the coming days" [1]. President Trump has reportedly approved a set of attack plans, although sources stress he has not yet made a final decision to execute them [2]. When asked directly, the President stated he "may or may not" strike Iran [3]. One report alleges these plans have been greenlit without an effort to seek congressional approval [4].

**References**
[1] US Officials Prepare for Possible Strike on Iran in Coming Days, https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-06-19/us-officials-prepare-for-strike-on-iran-in-the-coming-days?link_source=ta_bluesky_link&taid=6853648ebd022a0001faec52&utm_campaign=trueanthem&utm_content=business&utm_medium=social&utm_source=bluesky

[2] Trump approved attack plans for Iran — but hasn't made a final decision to strike, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/trump-attack-plans-iran-no-final-decision/

[3] US President Donald Trump says he 'may or may not' strike Iran as Israel's air war continues, https://news.sky.com/story/us-president-donald-trump-says-he-may-or-may-not-strike-iran-as-israels-air-war-continues-13385686

[4] Trump Reportedly Greenlights Plan for US Attack on Iran Without Congressional Approval, https://www.commondreams.org/news/trump-approves-iran-attack

**Topic 1.2: White House Deliberations & Internal Divisions**
Significant internal divisions are apparent within the administration's Iran policy circle. Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard has reportedly been sidelined from key discussions on Israel and Iran, with a scheduled Senate Intelligence briefing being postponed [1]. President Trump is reportedly focused on operational details, pressing aides on the effectiveness of the "bunker-buster" bomb plan; his hesitation to launch a strike is attributed to these specific doubts [2]. Tensions are also noted between the President’s public stance and U.S. intelligence assessments of Iran's nuclear progress [3]. In a separate report, Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth has allegedly been frozen out of Iran planning entirely [4].

**References**
[1] Tulsi Gabbard sidelined in Trump administration discussions on Israel and Iran, https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/trump-administration/tulsi-gabbard-sidelined-trump-administration-discussions-israel-iran-rcna212702

[2] Trump presses aides on whether bunker-buster plan to bomb Iran will work, https://www.axios.com/2025/06/18/trump-bunker-buster-bomb-iran-nuclear-program

[3] Trump and U.S. intelligence appear at odds over Iran's nuclear progress, https://www.nbcnews.com/world/iran/us-intelligence-assessment-irans-nuclear-program-remains-unchanged-rcna213879

[4] Trump Reportedly Freezes Out His Defense Secretary in Iran Planning: 'Nobody Is Talking to Hegseth', https://www.latintimes.com/trump-reportedly-freezes-out-his-defense-secretary-iran-planning-nobody-talking-hegseth-585313

**Topic 1.3: Diplomatic Engagement & International Reactions**
The rising tensions are triggering direct diplomatic and security measures. The United States has begun evacuating some diplomatic personnel from its embassy in Israel as the regional conflict continues to intensify [1]. In a notable diplomatic engagement, President Trump discussed the Israel-Iran conflict with the Pakistan Army Chief [2]. Meanwhile, an Israeli official identified as "Gallant" was quoted stating that the U.S. "has an obligation to assist Israel's operation in Iran," signaling clear expectations from a key ally [3].

**References**
[1] US starts evacuating some diplomats from its embassy in Israel as Iran conflict intensifies, https://apnews.com/article/embassy-israel-iran-united-states-7b4ebf294f390b47a5174413d3ef2682

### **Area 2: Legal & Judicial Affairs**

**Topic 2.1: Supreme Court Decisions & Impacts**
A recent Supreme Court decision has upheld a Tennessee law that bans transition-related healthcare for minors, prompting significant and critical reaction [1]. The ruling, known as the *Skrmetti* decision, is being described by critics as a move that has "undermined gender equality" and damaged the 14th amendment [1]. One op-ed from a parent of a child at the center of the case described their family’s heartbreak [2], while other advocacy groups warn the ruling will cause "untold harm" [3].

**References**
[1] The US supreme court just undermined gender equality - The Skrmetti decision upholding Tennessee’s ban on transition-related healthcare for minors deprives children and batters the 14th amendment, https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2025/jun/19/us-supreme-court-gender-equality

[2] My Daughter Was at the Center of the Supreme Court Case on Trans Care. Our Hearts Are Broken., https://www.nytimes.com/2025/06/18/opinion/supreme-court-trans-care.html?unlocked_article_code=1.P08.eIpO.tCDn4Remjkjb&smid=re-nytopinion

[3] Warnings of 'Untold Harm' After US Supreme Court Rules Against Trans Youth, https://www.commondreams.org/news/supreme-court-transgender-youth

**Topic 2.2: Federal Litigation Involving the Administration**
The administration is facing multiple, significant legal developments. In one case, a U.S. judge invalidated a rule from the previous administration that had sought to protect privacy for abortions [1]. Concurrently, an appeals court ruled that the Department of Justice cannot represent President Trump in the appeal of the E. Jean Carroll defamation case [2]. The President is also seeking to be removed as a defendant in a New Hampshire lawsuit that challenges his executive order concerning transgender athletes [3].

**References**
[1] US judge invalidates Biden rule protecting privacy for abortions, https://www.reuters.com/business/healthcare-pharmaceuticals/us-judge-invalidates-biden-rule-protecting-privacy-abortions-2025-06-18/

### **Area 3: Economic & Fiscal Policy**

**Topic 3.1: Entitlement Solvency and Economic Indicators**
Official projections for the long-term solvency of Social Security and Medicare have worsened, with the dates for insolvency now forecast to arrive sooner than previously expected [1]. The accelerated timeline is attributed to rising health care costs and a "new SSA law," though details of the law are not specified in available reporting. The finances of Social Security in particular are reported to have "eroded further," increasing the risk of future benefit cuts for millions of Americans [2]. Separate reports on general economic conditions are limited but point to growing wealth concentration, noting that the U.S. generated over 1,000 new millionaires per day last year [3].

**References**
[1] Medicare and Social Security go-broke dates pushed up due to rising health care costs, new SSA law, https://apnews.com/article/social-security-medicare-trust-fund-trump-74e13292f510739724a555d7ded7c1a3

### **Area 4: Executive Branch: Policy & Governance**

**Topic 4.1: Health, Science, & Social Policy**
The administration is implementing major changes in public health that are drawing sharp criticism. The new vaccine committee formed by HHS Secretary Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. is reportedly staffed with members who have limited publication records on vaccines, a move described in the journal *Science* as a "purge" resulting in a "major loss of expertise" [1]. In a separate action, the administration is moving to cut a specialized suicide prevention service for LGBTQ+ youth [2]. These moves coincide with reports of a potential "brain drain" as U.S. academics increasingly seek employment abroad [3].

**References**
[1] The members of RFK Jr.’s new vaccine committee have published little on vaccines | Purge at immunization panel represents a major loss of expertise, as measured by scientific papers, https://www.science.org/content/article/members-rfk-jr-s-new-vaccine-committee-have-published-little-vaccines

**Topic 4.2: Immigration & Homeland Security**
The administration is executing a multi-front strategy on immigration and security. New State Department rules now mandate social media screening for all student visa applicants [1], while physical border infrastructure is being expanded through a new $300 million contract for wall construction in southern Arizona [2]. Internally, a power struggle is developing, with Homeland Security Secretary Kristi Noem reportedly demanding greater direct control over FEMA and departmental funds, a move sources claim could slow disaster response [3]. Enforcement actions are also drawing scrutiny, such as a case where ICE detained a green-card holder who was returning from a visit to their son serving in the U.S. Air Force [4].

**References**

[4] ICE detains green card-holder returning from visit to son in US Air Force, https://www.newsweek.com/ice-detains-green-card-holder-returning-visit-son-us-air-force-2087397

**Topic 4.3: Environmental & Regulatory Rollbacks**
The administration is actively working to reverse key environmental regulations. The Environmental Protection Agency is set to "reconsider" the ban on cancer-causing asbestos, a move characterized by one outlet as an attempt to "bring back asbestos" [1, 2]. Separately, a report warns of a potential long-term agricultural crisis, suggesting that "Children born now may live in a world where the US can only produce half as much of its key food crops," although the direct cause for this projection is not detailed [3].

**References**

A major legislative priority for the administration, referred to as "Trump's 'big bill'," is advancing through the Senate via the reconciliation process [1]. Republican leadership is reported to be "aggressively" courting GOP holdouts on Medicaid to ensure the bill has enough support to pass [2]. The legislation is raising fiscal alarms in some states; Colorado lawmakers have been warned the bill could create a "billion-dollar budget crunch" for the state [3].

Tensions between Congress and the executive branch are escalating across multiple fronts. In a striking personal account, Senator Alex Padilla (D-CA) published an op-ed titled, "Senator Padilla: The Trump Administration Handcuffed Me, but I Refuse to Stay Silent," though specific details of the incident are not provided in the headline [1]. Direct confrontations are occurring in hearings as well; Rep. - The title should be simply "DAILY BRIEFING", nothing else, and followed by a space line. 

- The first-level headers (areas) should be in the format of "## 1. Ecnomic Policy and Trade Relations", using simple numbering, and upper case only for the first letter of each word. 

- The second-level headers (topics) should be in the format of "### 1.1 Tariffs and Market Reactions". 

- Citations in the text should be inserted properly. Every citation should be inserted directly after the phrases or sentences referring to that citation. Do not lump all citations at the end of the paragraph. And remember to add a space between the last word and the citation bracket. Example: "Financial markets have experienced severe turbulence following President Trump's global tariff implementation, with the S&P 500 heading toward bear market territory [1] and the Dow plummeting over 700 points [2]. Prominent financial figures have issued warnings, with Trump supporter Bill Ackman characterizing the situation as an "economic nuclear winter" [3] and JPMorgan CEO Jamie Dimon warning that tariffs will boost inflation and slow the economy [4]." 

In the reference list, at the end of each reference line, there should always be two spaces, "  ". This is a convenient way to start a new line for Markdown renderer.

Right after you finish printing the file step8.md, please output the end mark **exactly** as follows: two empty lines, and then a line: "==========Output File End============", without the quote marks.

It is very important to use this pair of marks **only** as the start mark and the end mark of your output file `step8.md`, as I said above. This pair should appear **precisely once** in your whole answer. **Never** mention them elsewhere, especially when explaining your edits. Otherwise, you will mess up with my output parsing script.

## 3. Economic and Fiscal Policy

### 3.1. Entitlement Solvency and Economic Indicators
Official projections for the long-term solvency of Social Security and Medicare have worsened, with the dates for insolvency now forecast to arrive sooner than previously expected [1]. The accelerated timeline is attributed to rising health care costs and a "new SSA law," though details of the law are not specified in available reporting. The finances of Social Security in particular are reported to have "eroded further," increasing the risk of future benefit cuts for millions of Americans [2]. Separate reports on general economic conditions are limited but point to growing wealth concentration, noting that the U.S. generated over 1,000 new millionaires per day last year [3].

## 4. Executive Branch: Policy and Governance

### 4.1. Health, Science, and Social Policy
The administration is implementing major changes in public health that are drawing sharp criticism. The new vaccine committee formed by HHS Secretary Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. is reportedly staffed with members who have limited publication records on vaccines, a move described in the journal *Science* as a "purge" resulting in a "major loss of expertise" [1]. In a separate action, the administration is moving to cut a specialized suicide prevention service for LGBTQ+ youth [2]. These moves coincide with reports of a potential "brain drain" as U.S. academics increasingly seek employment abroad [3].

The administration is executing a multi-front strategy on immigration and security. Internally, a power struggle is developing, with Homeland Security Secretary Kristi Noem reportedly demanding greater direct control over FEMA and departmental funds, a move sources claim could slow disaster response [3]. Enforcement actions are also drawing scrutiny, such as a case where ICE detained a green-card holder who was returning from a visit to their son serving in the U.S. Air Force [4].
